-  "AIDescription": "### General Description\nEnriches URL entities with traffic
rank information from the Alexa Web Information Service (AWIS). This action 
helps security analysts determine the popularity and potential risk of a domain 
by retrieving its global traffic rank. If a URL's rank exceeds a specified 
threshold (indicating it is less popular or potentially rare), the action marks 
the entity as suspicious and generates a security insight.\n\n### Parameters 
Description\n| Parameter | Type | Mandatory | Description |\n| :--- | :--- | 
:--- | :--- |\n| Threshold | Integer | Yes | The numerical rank value used to 
evaluate risk. If the retrieved Alexa rank is greater than this threshold 
(meaning the site is less popular), the entity is flagged as suspicious. 
|\n\n### Additional Notes\n* The action requires valid AWS credentials (Access 
Key ID and Secret Access Key) configured in the Alexa integration settings.\n* 
Alexa ranks are inverse: a rank of 1 is the most popular site globally. A higher
numerical rank indicates a less frequently visited site.\n\n### Flow 
Description\n1. **Authentication**: Initializes the Alexa Manager using the 
provided AWS credentials from the integration configuration.\n2. **Entity 
Filtering**: Identifies all URL entities within the current scope.\n3. **Data 
Retrieval**: For each URL, it queries the Alexa Web Information Service to fetch
the 'Rank' response group.\n4. **Enrichment**: Updates the entity's additional 
properties with the `Alexa_Rank` and marks the entity as enriched.\n5. **Risk 
Assessment**: Compares the retrieved rank against the user-defined `Threshold`. 
If the rank is higher than the threshold, the entity is marked as 
suspicious.\n6. **Insight Generation**: Creates an entity insight for suspicious
URLs stating they were found suspicious by Alexa.\n7. **Reporting**: Updates the
entities in the SOAR platform and provides a summary message and a detailed JSON
result containing the raw traffic data.",

   "AIDescription": "### General Description\nThe **HTTPS Information Lookup** 
action queries the MXToolBox API to verify if a website URL responds securely 
via SSL encryption. It retrieves details about the SSL certificate, specifically
identifying the certificate authorities associated with the domain.\n\n### 
Parameters Description\nThis action does not have any input parameters. It 
relies on the integration's global configuration (API Root, API Key, and Verify 
SSL).\n\n### Additional Notes\nThe action uses the `get_domain_from_entity` 
utility to ensure the API receives a domain string rather than a full URL. If an
error occurs for a specific entity, the action logs the error and continues 
processing the remaining entities.\n\n### Flow Description\n1. **Entity 
Filtering**: The action identifies all `URL` entities within the current 
context.\n2. **Domain Extraction**: For each URL, it extracts the base domain 
name.\n3. **API Query**: It sends a request to the MXToolBox HTTPS lookup 
endpoint for each domain.\n4. **Data Processing**: It parses the response to 
extract the names of the certificate authorities.\n5. **Reporting**: It creates 
a data table named 'HTTPS Information Lookup Result' and attaches the raw JSON 
response to the action results.",

Retrieves NetWitness configuration (Concentrator/Decoder URIs and credentials)

primary index.\n4. **Packaging**: Compresses the generated feed files (CSV and
